## MANDATORY: Use Sourcegraph Code Search Tools BEFORE Any Code Changes

You have Sourcegraph MCP tools available (keyword_search, nls_search, list_files, read_file, go_to_definition, find_references, deepsearch, deepsearch_read). You MUST use them as your primary code discovery method.

Use `list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.

**CRITICAL — TWO-PHASE WORKFLOW:**

### Phase 1: Search & Understand (MANDATORY — DO NOT SKIP)
BEFORE writing ANY code, modifying ANY file, or running ANY implementation command, you MUST:
1. Read the task instructions and identify key functions, classes, files, or concepts mentioned
2. Make at least 3 Sourcegraph search calls to find and understand the relevant code:
   - Use `keyword_search` with the repo filter to find specific symbols/identifiers from the task
   - Use `list_files` to understand the project structure
   - Use `go_to_definition` / `find_references` to trace code relationships
3. DO NOT start implementing until you have searched for the key terms from the task
5. Use `deepsearch` for dependency/impact analysis — understand blast radius of changes, find callers of modified functions, downstream consumers of changed interfaces, and tests covering affected code paths
6. `deepsearch` returns a polling link, NOT immediate results. After calling it, continue working with other tools for 30-60 seconds, then call `deepsearch_read` with the polling link
7. Retry `deepsearch_read` at least 3 times — Deep Search takes 50-120 seconds to complete
8. For code review tasks: the PR diff alone does NOT show full impact. Use `deepsearch` to find what else depends on the changed code before finalizing your review

### Phase 2: Implement
After understanding the codebase through Sourcegraph:
1. Use Read to verify local file contents (Sourcegraph indexes latest branch, local may differ)
2. If Sourcegraph shows different code than local, TRUST THE LOCAL CODE
3. Make your code changes — stop searching, focus on implementation

See CLAUDE.md for the complete tool selection guide.

# Team Handoff: Envoy ext_authz Filter

You are taking over ownership of the **ext_authz HTTP filter** from a departing team member. Your task is to produce a comprehensive handoff document that will help you (and future maintainers) understand this component.

## Context

The ext_authz filter is one of Envoy's authorization extensions. Your predecessor maintained it for the past year but is moving to a different project. You need to quickly build a working mental model of this component.

## Your Task

Explore the Envoy codebase and produce a handoff document at `/logs/agent/onboarding.md` covering the following sections:

### 1. Purpose
What does the ext_authz filter do? What problems does it solve? When would someone use it?

### 2. Dependencies
- **Upstream dependencies**: What other Envoy components or libraries does ext_authz depend on?
- **Downstream consumers**: What uses or integrates with ext_authz? How is it configured in Envoy's filter chain?

### 3. Relevant Components
List the most important source files for this filter. For each file, explain its role (e.g., "configuration parsing", "request handling", "gRPC client implementation").

### 4. Failure Modes
What can go wrong? What are common failure scenarios? How does the filter handle errors (e.g., authorization service unavailable, timeout, network failure)?

### 5. Testing
How is this filter tested? Where are the tests located? Are there integration tests, unit tests, or both?

### 6. Debugging
If something goes wrong with ext_authz in production, how would you debug it? What logs, metrics, or traces would you look at?

## Deliverable

Write your findings to `/logs/agent/onboarding.md` using the following structure:

```
# ext_authz Filter Handoff Document

## 1. Purpose
[Your findings here]

## 2. Dependencies
### Upstream Dependencies
[What ext_authz depends on]

### Downstream Consumers
[What depends on ext_authz]

## 3. Relevant Components
- **path/to/file.cc**: [Role/responsibility]
- **path/to/file.h**: [Role/responsibility]
...

## 4. Failure Modes
[Failure scenarios and error handling]

## 5. Testing
[Test locations, test types, how to run tests]

## 6. Debugging
[Debugging strategies, observability]
```

## Guidelines

- Be specific. Reference actual file paths, class names, function names.
- Focus on understanding the **system's behavior**, not just describing the code.
- This is analysis only — do not modify any code.
- Use code search and file exploration tools to explore the codebase efficiently.

66-assistanttext-
The handoff document has been written to `/logs/agent/onboarding.md`. Here's a summary of what it covers:

**1. Purpose**: The ext_authz filter delegates authorization to an external service via gRPC or HTTP. It intercepts requests, sends `CheckRequest` protobufs, and acts on OK/Denied/Error verdicts.

**2. Dependencies**: Maps 12+ upstream dependencies (gRPC/HTTP async clients, cluster manager, runtime, stats, filter state, router, tracing, matchers, mutation rules, protobufs) and downstream consumers (HCM filter chains, per-route config, access logging, dynamic metadata consumers).

**3. Relevant Components**: Documents all key files across three layers:
- HTTP filter: `ext_authz.h/.cc`, `config.h/.cc` (5 files)
- Common library: `ext_authz.h`, `ext_authz_grpc_impl.h/.cc`, `ext_authz_http_impl.h/.cc`, `check_request_utils.h/.cc` (7 files)
- Network filter: `ext_authz.h/.cc`, `config.h/.cc` (4 files)

**4. Failure Modes**: Covers 8 failure scenarios including authz unavailability (fail-open vs fail-closed), denial, CDS cluster removal, invalid mutations, header limit exhaustion, filter disabled, per-route override failures, and mid-call stream destruction.

**5. Testing**: Catalogs unit tests (7 files), integration tests (2 files), fuzz tests (3 files), and mock/test utilities (4 files), with Bazel commands to run them.

**6. Debugging**: Documents 11 stats counters, trace-level log messages, tracing tags (`ext_authz_status`), filter state fields (`ExtAuthzLoggingInfo`), response flags (`UF`), response code details, dynamic metadata, and a step-by-step debugging workflow.

27. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# ext_authz Filter Handoff Document\n\n## 1. Purpose\n\nThe ext_authz filter is an **external authorization** filter for Envoy that delegates request authorization decisions to an external service. It exists as both an **HTTP filter** (`envoy.filters.http.ext_authz`) and a **network (TCP) filter** (`envoy.filters.network.ext_authz`), both sharing a common client library.\n\n### What it does\n\nBefore a request reaches the upstream service, the ext_authz filter intercepts it and sends an authorization check request (a `CheckRequest` protobuf) to a configurable external authorization server. The authz server inspects request attributes (headers, path, source/destination IPs, TLS info, request body, metadata) and returns one of three verdicts:\n\n- **OK**: The request is authorized. The authz server can optionally mutate request headers, add/remove query parameters, set response headers, and inject dynamic metadata.\n- **Denied**: The request is rejected. The filter sends a local reply (configurable status code, body, and headers) back to the client without forwarding to the upstream.\n- **Error**: The authz server was unreachable or returned an error. Behavior depends on the `failure_mode_allow` configuration (fail-open vs. fail-closed).\n\n### When to use it\n\n- Enforcing authorization policies (RBAC, OPA, custom authz logic) external to Envoy.\n- Integrating with third-party authz systems (e.g., Open Policy Agent, Istio authz).\n- Adding per-request authentication/authorization without modifying application code.\n- Implementing request enrichment -- the authz server can add headers, modify query params, and inject metadata on approved requests.\n\n### Communication Modes\n\nThe filter supports two backend protocols for communicating with the authz service:\n\n1. **gRPC** (`grpc_service`): Uses the `envoy.service.auth.v3.Authorization.Check` RPC method. The authz server returns a structured `CheckResponse` protobuf with explicit `OkHttpResponse`, `DeniedHttpResponse`, or `ErrorResponse` fields. This is the richer protocol with full control over response mutations.\n2. **HTTP** (`http_service`): Sends a raw HTTP request to an authz cluster. An HTTP 200 means OK; 5xx means Error; anything else (e.g., 403) means Denied. Response header matching rules determine which headers are forwarded upstream or back to the client.\n\n## 2. Dependencies\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe ext_authz filter depends on the following Envoy subsystems and libraries:\n\n| Dependency | Purpose | Key Files |\n|---|---|---|\n| **gRPC async client** | Sends `CheckRequest` to gRPC authz servers | `envoy/grpc/async_client.h`, `envoy/grpc/async_client_manager.h`, `source/common/grpc/typed_async_client.h` |\n| **HTTP async client** | Sends HTTP requests to HTTP-based authz servers | `source/common/http/async_client_impl.h`, via `Upstream::ClusterManager` |\n| **Cluster Manager** | Resolves the authz server cluster, creates thread-local HTTP clients | `envoy/upstream/cluster_manager.h` |\n| **Runtime / Feature Flags** | `filter_enabled` fractional percent, `deny_at_disable`, runtime feature flags | `envoy/runtime/runtime.h`, `source/common/runtime/runtime_protos.h` |\n| **Stats** | Emits counters for ok/denied/error/disabled/failure_mode_allowed | `envoy/stats/scope.h`, `envoy/stats/stats_macros.h` |\n| **Filter State** | Stores `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` for access logging | `envoy/stream_info/filter_state.h` |\n| **Router / Route Config** | Per-route configuration (`FilterConfigPerRoute`), route cache clearing | `envoy/router/router.h`, `source/common/router/config_impl.h` |\n| **Tracing** | Propagates spans to the authz service call, sets trace tags | `envoy/tracing/tracer.h` |\n| **Matchers** | Header matching for allowed/disallowed headers, metadata matching | `source/common/common/matchers.h` |\n| **Mutation Rules** | Validates header mutations from authz responses | `source/extensions/filters/common/mutation_rules/mutation_rules.h` |\n| **Protobuf definitions** | `CheckRequest`, `CheckResponse`, `AttributeContext` | `envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.pb.h`, `envoy/service/auth/v3/attribute_context.pb.h` |\n| **Filter config protos** | `ExtAuthz`, `ExtAuthzPerRoute`, `HttpService`, `CheckSettings` | `envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/v3/ext_authz.pb.h` |\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n- **Envoy HTTP Connection Manager (HCM)**: The filter is registered as `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` and added to HCM filter chains. It implements `Http::StreamFilter` (both decoder and encoder).\n- **Envoy Network Filter Chain**: The TCP variant (`envoy.filters.network.ext_authz`) is added to network filter chains as a `Network::ReadFilter`.\n- **Per-route configuration**: Consumers configure `ExtAuthzPerRoute` on virtual hosts, routes, or weighted clusters to customize authorization behavior (disable checks, add context extensions, override the authz service endpoint).\n- **Access logging**: Downstream access log filters can read `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` from filter state (keyed by the filter config name) to log authz latency, bytes sent/received, gRPC status, and cluster info.\n- **Dynamic metadata consumers**: Other filters in the chain can read metadata set under the `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` namespace by the authz server's response (e.g., for use in routing, rate limiting, or logging).\n\n## 3. Relevant Components\n\n### HTTP Filter (main filter)\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.h`**: Core header defining `FilterConfig`, `FilterConfigPerRoute`, `Filter`, `ExtAuthzFilterStats`, and `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo`. `Filter` implements `Http::StreamFilter` and `RequestCallbacks`. `FilterConfig` holds all parsed configuration. `FilterConfigPerRoute` enables per-route overrides (disable, context extensions, per-route service).\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.cc`**: Main filter implementation. Key methods:\n  - `decodeHeaders()` (~line 398): Entry point. Checks per-route flags, decides whether to buffer body, initiates the check call.\n  - `decodeData()` (~line 451): Buffers request body until `max_request_bytes` or end-of-stream.\n  - `initiateCall()` (~line 275): Builds the `CheckRequest` protobuf, merges per-route config, fills metadata context, and calls `client_->check()`.\n  - `onComplete()` (~line 631): Callback from the authz client. Handles OK/Denied/Error responses, applies header mutations, query parameter mutations, sets response flags.\n  - `createPerRouteGrpcClient()` / `createPerRouteHttpClient()`: Create per-route authz clients when per-route service overrides are configured.\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config.h`**: Factory registration. `ExtAuthzFilterConfig` extends `Common::FactoryBase`. Registered as `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` (legacy name: `envoy.ext_authz`).\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config.cc`**: Factory implementation. `createFilterFactoryFromProtoWithServerContextTyped()` creates either a `GrpcClientImpl` or `RawHttpClientImpl` based on the config, then wraps it in a `Filter`.\n\n### Common Library (shared between HTTP and TCP filters)\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz.h`**: Defines the `Client` interface (with `check()` and `cancel()` methods), `RequestCallbacks`, `Response` struct (with `CheckStatus::OK/Denied/Error`), `ResponseCodeDetails`, `TracingConstants`, and `Headers` constants (e.g., `x-envoy-auth-failure-mode-allowed`, `x-envoy-auth-partial-body`).\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl.h` / `.cc`**: `GrpcClientImpl` -- gRPC client using `Grpc::AsyncClient`. Sends `CheckRequest`, handles `CheckResponse` in `onSuccess()`/`onFailure()`. Maps gRPC status to `CheckStatus`. Copies header mutations from `OkHttpResponse`, `DeniedHttpResponse`, or `ErrorResponse`.\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl.h` / `.cc`**: `RawHttpClientImpl` -- HTTP client using `Http::AsyncClient`. Sends an HTTP request to the authz cluster. `toResponse()` maps HTTP status codes: 200 = OK, 5xx = Error, else = Denied. Uses header matchers to select which response headers to forward upstream or to the client.\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/check_request_utils.h` / `.cc`**: `CheckRequestUtils` -- utility class that builds `CheckRequest` protobufs. `createHttpCheck()` populates the `AttributeContext` with source/destination peers, HTTP request attributes (method, path, headers, body), TLS info, peer certificates, and metadata. `createTcpCheck()` does the same for TCP connections.\n\n### Network (TCP) Filter\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/ext_authz.h` / `.cc`**: TCP variant. Implements `Network::ReadFilter`. Only supports gRPC. Calls `checkRequestUtils::createTcpCheck()` and sends the check on `onNewConnection()`.\n- **`source/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/config.h` / `.cc`**: Factory for the TCP filter, registered as `envoy.filters.network.ext_authz`.\n\n### Supporting\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/mutation_rules/mutation_rules.h` / `.cc`**: `Checker` class that validates header mutations against configurable rules (allow/disallow specific header operations).\n\n## 4. Failure Modes\n\n### 4.1 Authorization Service Unavailable / Timeout\n\n**Trigger**: The authz service cluster is unreachable, the gRPC call fails, or the HTTP request to the authz service returns 5xx or times out.\n\n**Behavior**: The `Client` returns `CheckStatus::Error`.\n\n- If `failure_mode_allow: true` (fail-open): The request is **allowed through**. The `failure_mode_allowed` counter is incremented. If `failure_mode_allow_header_add: true`, an `x-envoy-auth-failure-mode-allowed: true` header is added to the request so the upstream knows the authz check was skipped.\n- If `failure_mode_allow: false` (fail-closed, **default**): The request is **rejected** with a local reply. The status code is `status_on_error` (default: 403 Forbidden). The response detail is `ext_authz_error`. The `UnauthorizedExternalService` response flag is set.\n- For gRPC error responses with `error_response` present, custom status code, body, headers_to_set, and headers_to_append from the error response are applied (if `validate_mutations` passes).\n\n**Stats incremented**: `error`, and (if applicable) `failure_mode_allowed`.\n\n### 4.2 Authorization Denied\n\n**Trigger**: The authz server explicitly denies the request (non-OK gRPC status without `error_response`, or non-200/non-5xx HTTP status).\n\n**Behavior**: A local reply is sent to the client with:\n- Status code from the `DeniedHttpResponse` (default 403).\n- Body from the denial response (truncated to `max_denied_response_body_bytes` if set).\n- Headers from the denial response's `headers_to_set` field.\n- The `UnauthorizedExternalService` response flag is set. Response detail: `ext_authz_denied`.\n\n**Stats incremented**: `denied`.\n\n### 4.3 Cluster Removed (CDS)\n\n**Trigger**: The authz cluster configured in `http_service.server_uri.cluster` is removed via CDS while the filter is running.\n\n**Behavior** (HTTP client): `RawHttpClientImpl::check()` returns an error response immediately when `cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(cluster)` returns `nullptr`. This is treated as `CheckStatus::Error`.\n\n### 4.4 Invalid Authz Response\n\n**Trigger**: The authz server returns headers or query parameters that fail validation (when `validate_mutations: true`), such as invalid header names/values or invalid URL-encoded query parameters.\n\n**Behavior**: The request is rejected with 500 Internal Server Error. Response detail: `ext_authz_invalid`. The `invalid` stat is incremented.\n\n### 4.5 Response Header Limits Exceeded\n\n**Trigger**: Mutations from the authz response would cause request or response headers to exceed the configured header count or byte-size limits.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- For request header mutations: If `headersWithinLimits()` fails after a mutation, the response is rejected (500). `request_header_limits_reached` stat is incremented.\n- For response header mutations (encode path): If `enforce_response_header_limits: true` and limits are exceeded, a 500 local reply is sent. `response_header_limits_reached` stat is incremented.\n- For denied/error responses: Excess headers are silently dropped when `enforce_response_header_limits: true`. `omitted_response_headers` stat is incremented.\n\n### 4.6 Filter Disabled\n\n**Trigger**: `filter_enabled` evaluates to false (runtime fractional percent) or `filter_enabled_metadata` doesn't match.\n\n**Behavior**: If `deny_at_disable: true`, the request is denied (status = `status_on_error`). Otherwise, the filter is bypassed and the request continues. The `disabled` stat is incremented.\n\n### 4.7 Per-Route Service Override Failure\n\n**Trigger**: A per-route `grpc_service` or `http_service` override is configured but the client creation fails.\n\n**Behavior**: Falls back to the default (globally configured) authz client. A warning-level log is emitted.\n\n### 4.8 Request Destroyed Mid-Call\n\n**Trigger**: The downstream connection is closed or the stream is reset while the authz check is in flight.\n\n**Behavior**: `Filter::onDestroy()` calls `client_->cancel()` to cancel the in-flight gRPC or HTTP request if the state is `State::Calling`.\n\n## 5. Testing\n\n### Unit Tests\n\n| Test File | Scope |\n|---|---|\n| `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_test.cc` | Core HTTP filter unit tests. Tests `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, `onComplete()` for all response types (OK, Denied, Error). Tests header mutations, query parameter mutations, per-route config, `failure_mode_allow`, dynamic metadata, body buffering, and validation. Parametrized over gRPC/HTTP client types. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config_test.cc` | Config factory tests. Tests proto validation, factory creation for gRPC and HTTP service configs. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl_test.cc` | gRPC client implementation tests. Tests `check()`, `onSuccess()`, `onFailure()`, response parsing, tracing tag setting. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl_test.cc` | HTTP client implementation tests. Tests request construction, response parsing, header matching, cluster-not-found handling. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/check_request_utils_test.cc` | Tests `CheckRequest` protobuf construction from HTTP/TCP request attributes. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/ext_authz_test.cc` | TCP filter unit tests. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/config_test.cc` | TCP filter config factory tests. |\n\n### Integration Tests\n\n| Test File | Scope |\n|---|---|\n| `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_integration_test.cc` | End-to-end tests with a real gRPC authz server. Tests OK/Denied/Error flows, header mutations, body buffering, failure mode, metadata, timeouts, response header limits, per-route overrides. Parametrized over IP version, gRPC client type, and filter config variants. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/ext_authz_integration_test.cc` | End-to-end tests for the TCP filter with a real gRPC server. |\n\n### Fuzz Tests\n\n| Test File | Scope |\n|---|---|\n| `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_fuzz_test.cc` | Fuzz testing for the gRPC filter path. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_fuzz_test.cc` | Fuzz testing for the HTTP filter path. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/ext_authz_fuzz_test.cc` | Fuzz testing for the TCP filter. |\n\n### Test Mocks\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/mocks.h` / `.cc`**: Mock `Client` implementation for unit testing the filter without a real authz server.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/test_common.h` / `.cc`**: Shared test utilities.\n\n### Running Tests\n\nTests are built and run via Bazel:\n```bash\n# HTTP filter unit tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz:ext_authz_test\n\n# HTTP filter integration tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz:ext_authz_integration_test\n\n# Common library tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz:...\n\n# TCP filter tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz:...\n```\n\n## 6. Debugging\n\n### Stats / Metrics\n\nThe filter emits counters under the prefix `ext_authz.<stat_prefix>.` (where `stat_prefix` is configurable, default empty yields `ext_authz.`):\n\n| Stat Name | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `ok` | Requests approved by the authz service. |\n| `denied` | Requests denied by the authz service. |\n| `error` | Authz service returned an error or was unreachable. |\n| `disabled` | Requests where the filter was disabled (via `filter_enabled`). |\n| `failure_mode_allowed` | Requests allowed through despite authz errors (fail-open). |\n| `invalid` | Responses rejected due to invalid mutations (`validate_mutations`). |\n| `ignored_dynamic_metadata` | Dynamic metadata from authz ignored (`enable_dynamic_metadata_ingestion: false`). |\n| `filter_state_name_collision` | Filter state key collision (another filter already set data at this name). |\n| `omitted_response_headers` | Response headers from authz that were dropped due to header limits. |\n| `request_header_limits_reached` | Request header mutations exceeded limits. |\n| `response_header_limits_reached` | Response header mutations exceeded limits. |\n\nWhen `charge_cluster_response_stats: true` (default), the filter also charges per-cluster stats under the authz cluster's scope: `ext_authz.ok`, `ext_authz.denied`, `ext_authz.error`, `ext_authz.invalid`, `ext_authz.failure_mode_allowed`.\n\n**Key diagnostic**: A spike in `error` + `failure_mode_allowed` indicates authz service instability. A spike in `denied` may indicate a policy change or misconfiguration. Monitor `invalid` if `validate_mutations` is enabled.\n\n### Logging\n\nThe filter uses the `ext_authz` log component (`Logger::Id::ext_authz`). Enable trace-level logging with:\n```\n--component-log-level ext_authz:trace\n```\n\nKey log messages:\n- `trace`: \"ext_authz filter calling authorization server.\" -- call initiated.\n- `trace`: \"ext_authz filter added header(s) to the request/response\" -- header mutations applied.\n- `debug`: \"ext_authz filter is buffering the request\" -- body buffering started.\n- `debug`: \"ext_authz is clearing route cache\" -- route cache cleared after header mutations.\n- `trace`: \"ext_authz filter allowed the request with error\" -- fail-open triggered.\n- `trace`: \"ext_authz filter rejected the request. Response status code: ...\" -- request denied.\n- `warn`: \"ext_authz filter: failed to create per-route gRPC/HTTP client...\" -- per-route client creation failure.\n\nFor the HTTP client, relevant logs are under `Logger::Id::config`.\nFor the gRPC client, relevant logs are under `Logger::Id::ext_authz`.\n\n### Tracing\n\nThe filter propagates tracing spans to the authz service call. The gRPC client passes the parent span to the async gRPC call. The HTTP client creates a child span named `async <cluster_name> egress`.\n\nTrace tags set by the filter:\n- `ext_authz_status`: `ext_authz_ok`, `ext_authz_unauthorized`, or `ext_authz_error`.\n- `ext_authz_http_status`: HTTP status code (HTTP client only).\n\n### Filter State\n\nWhen `emit_filter_state_stats: true` or `filter_metadata` is configured, the filter stores `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` in the request's filter state (keyed by the filter config name). This object exposes:\n- `latency_us`: Latency of the authz call in microseconds.\n- `bytesSent` / `bytesReceived`: Wire bytes for the authz call (gRPC via Envoy gRPC only).\n- `clusterInfo`: The authz cluster info.\n- `upstreamHost`: The specific authz host that handled the request.\n- `grpcStatus`: The gRPC status code from the authz response.\n\nThese values are accessible from access log formatters that support filter state field lookup.\n\n### Response Flags\n\nThe filter sets the `UF` (UnauthorizedExternalService) response flag when a request is denied or encounters an error. This appears in access logs as `UF`.\n\n### Response Code Details\n\n| Detail String | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `ext_authz_denied` | Request was explicitly denied by the authz service. |\n| `ext_authz_error` | Authz service returned an error and fail-closed is active. |\n| `ext_authz_invalid` | Authz response contained invalid mutations. |\n\n### Dynamic Metadata\n\nOn OK responses, the authz server can inject dynamic metadata under the `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` namespace. This metadata includes an auto-added `ext_authz_duration` field (in milliseconds) and any metadata from the authz response's `dynamic_metadata` field. Other filters (rate limiting, routing, access logging) can consume this metadata.\n\n### Common Debugging Workflow\n\n1. Check stats: Look at `ext_authz.ok`, `ext_authz.denied`, `ext_authz.error` to understand the distribution of outcomes.\n2. Check access logs: Look for the `UF` response flag and `ext_authz_denied`/`ext_authz_error` response code details.\n3. Enable trace logging: Set `--component-log-level ext_authz:trace` to see the full request/response flow.\n4. Check the authz server: Verify the authz cluster is healthy via admin endpoint (`/clusters`). Look for connection failures, timeouts, or 5xx responses.\n5. Check tracing: Use distributed tracing to see the authz call latency and status tags.\n6. Check filter state: If `emit_filter_state_stats` is enabled, inspect latency and bytes via access log formatters.\n7. For header mutation issues: Enable `validate_mutations: true` and monitor `invalid` stats. Check trace logs for \"Rejected invalid header\" or \"Ignoring invalid header\" messages.\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/onboarding.md"

  "content": "# ext_authz Filter Handoff Document\n\n## 1. Purpose\n\nThe ext_authz filter is an **external authorization** filter for Envoy that delegates request authorization decisions to an external service. It exists as both an **HTTP filter** (`envoy.filters.http.ext_authz`) and a **network (TCP) filter** (`envoy.filters.network.ext_authz`), both sharing a common client library.\n\n### What it does\n\nBefore a request reaches the upstream service, the ext_authz filter intercepts it and sends an authorization check request (a `CheckRequest` protobuf) to a configurable external authorization server. The authz server inspects request attributes (headers, path, source/destination IPs, TLS info, request body, metadata) and returns one of three verdicts:\n\n- **OK**: The request is authorized. The authz server can optionally mutate request headers, add/remove query parameters, set response headers, and inject dynamic metadata.\n- **Denied**: The request is rejected. The filter sends a local reply (configurable status code, body, and headers) back to the client without forwarding to the upstream.\n- **Error**: The authz server was unreachable or returned an error. Behavior depends on the `failure_mode_allow` configuration (fail-open vs. fail-closed).\n\n### When to use it\n\n- Enforcing authorization policies (RBAC, OPA, custom authz logic) external to Envoy.\n- Integrating with third-party authz systems (e.g., Open Policy Agent, Istio authz).\n- Adding per-request authentication/authorization without modifying application code.\n- Implementing request enrichment -- the authz server can add headers, modify query params, and inject metadata on approved requests.\n\n### Communication Modes\n\nThe filter supports two backend protocols for communicating with the authz service:\n\n1. **gRPC** (`grpc_service`): Uses the `envoy.service.auth.v3.Authorization.Check` RPC method. The authz server returns a structured `CheckResponse` protobuf with explicit `OkHttpResponse`, `DeniedHttpResponse`, or `ErrorResponse` fields. This is the richer protocol with full control over response mutations.\n2. **HTTP** (`http_service`): Sends a raw HTTP request to an authz cluster. An HTTP 200 means OK; 5xx means Error; anything else (e.g., 403) means Denied. Response header matching rules determine which headers are forwarded upstream or back to the client.\n\n## 2. Dependencies\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe ext_authz filter depends on the following Envoy subsystems and libraries:\n\n| Dependency | Purpose | Key Files |\n|---|---|---|\n| **gRPC async client** | Sends `CheckRequest` to gRPC authz servers | `envoy/grpc/async_client.h`, `envoy/grpc/async_client_manager.h`, `source/common/grpc/typed_async_client.h` |\n| **HTTP async client** | Sends HTTP requests to HTTP-based authz servers | `source/common/http/async_client_impl.h`, via `Upstream::ClusterManager` |\n| **Cluster Manager** | Resolves the authz server cluster, creates thread-local HTTP clients | `envoy/upstream/cluster_manager.h` |\n| **Runtime / Feature Flags** | `filter_enabled` fractional percent, `deny_at_disable`, runtime feature flags | `envoy/runtime/runtime.h`, `source/common/runtime/runtime_protos.h` |\n| **Stats** | Emits counters for ok/denied/error/disabled/failure_mode_allowed | `envoy/stats/scope.h`, `envoy/stats/stats_macros.h` |\n| **Filter State** | Stores `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` for access logging | `envoy/stream_info/filter_state.h` |\n| **Router / Route Config** | Per-route configuration (`FilterConfigPerRoute`), route cache clearing | `envoy/router/router.h`, `source/common/router/config_impl.h` |\n| **Tracing** | Propagates spans to the authz service call, sets trace tags | `envoy/tracing/tracer.h` |\n| **Matchers** | Header matching for allowed/disallowed headers, metadata matching | `source/common/common/matchers.h` |\n| **Mutation Rules** | Validates header mutations from authz responses | `source/extensions/filters/common/mutation_rules/mutation_rules.h` |\n| **Protobuf definitions** | `CheckRequest`, `CheckResponse`, `AttributeContext` | `envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.pb.h`, `envoy/service/auth/v3/attribute_context.pb.h` |\n| **Filter config protos** | `ExtAuthz`, `ExtAuthzPerRoute`, `HttpService`, `CheckSettings` | `envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/v3/ext_authz.pb.h` |\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n- **Envoy HTTP Connection Manager (HCM)**: The filter is registered as `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` and added to HCM filter chains. It implements `Http::StreamFilter` (both decoder and encoder).\n- **Envoy Network Filter Chain**: The TCP variant (`envoy.filters.network.ext_authz`) is added to network filter chains as a `Network::ReadFilter`.\n- **Per-route configuration**: Consumers configure `ExtAuthzPerRoute` on virtual hosts, routes, or weighted clusters to customize authorization behavior (disable checks, add context extensions, override the authz service endpoint).\n- **Access logging**: Downstream access log filters can read `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` from filter state (keyed by the filter config name) to log authz latency, bytes sent/received, gRPC status, and cluster info.\n- **Dynamic metadata consumers**: Other filters in the chain can read metadata set under the `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` namespace by the authz server's response (e.g., for use in routing, rate limiting, or logging).\n\n## 3. Relevant Components\n\n### HTTP Filter (main filter)\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.h`**: Core header defining `FilterConfig`, `FilterConfigPerRoute`, `Filter`, `ExtAuthzFilterStats`, and `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo`. `Filter` implements `Http::StreamFilter` and `RequestCallbacks`. `FilterConfig` holds all parsed configuration. `FilterConfigPerRoute` enables per-route overrides (disable, context extensions, per-route service).\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.cc`**: Main filter implementation. Key methods:\n  - `decodeHeaders()` (~line 398): Entry point. Checks per-route flags, decides whether to buffer body, initiates the check call.\n  - `decodeData()` (~line 451): Buffers request body until `max_request_bytes` or end-of-stream.\n  - `initiateCall()` (~line 275): Builds the `CheckRequest` protobuf, merges per-route config, fills metadata context, and calls `client_->check()`.\n  - `onComplete()` (~line 631): Callback from the authz client. Handles OK/Denied/Error responses, applies header mutations, query parameter mutations, sets response flags.\n  - `createPerRouteGrpcClient()` / `createPerRouteHttpClient()`: Create per-route authz clients when per-route service overrides are configured.\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config.h`**: Factory registration. `ExtAuthzFilterConfig` extends `Common::FactoryBase`. Registered as `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` (legacy name: `envoy.ext_authz`).\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config.cc`**: Factory implementation. `createFilterFactoryFromProtoWithServerContextTyped()` creates either a `GrpcClientImpl` or `RawHttpClientImpl` based on the config, then wraps it in a `Filter`.\n\n### Common Library (shared between HTTP and TCP filters)\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz.h`**: Defines the `Client` interface (with `check()` and `cancel()` methods), `RequestCallbacks`, `Response` struct (with `CheckStatus::OK/Denied/Error`), `ResponseCodeDetails`, `TracingConstants`, and `Headers` constants (e.g., `x-envoy-auth-failure-mode-allowed`, `x-envoy-auth-partial-body`).\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl.h` / `.cc`**: `GrpcClientImpl` -- gRPC client using `Grpc::AsyncClient`. Sends `CheckRequest`, handles `CheckResponse` in `onSuccess()`/`onFailure()`. Maps gRPC status to `CheckStatus`. Copies header mutations from `OkHttpResponse`, `DeniedHttpResponse`, or `ErrorResponse`.\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl.h` / `.cc`**: `RawHttpClientImpl` -- HTTP client using `Http::AsyncClient`. Sends an HTTP request to the authz cluster. `toResponse()` maps HTTP status codes: 200 = OK, 5xx = Error, else = Denied. Uses header matchers to select which response headers to forward upstream or to the client.\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/check_request_utils.h` / `.cc`**: `CheckRequestUtils` -- utility class that builds `CheckRequest` protobufs. `createHttpCheck()` populates the `AttributeContext` with source/destination peers, HTTP request attributes (method, path, headers, body), TLS info, peer certificates, and metadata. `createTcpCheck()` does the same for TCP connections.\n\n### Network (TCP) Filter\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/ext_authz.h` / `.cc`**: TCP variant. Implements `Network::ReadFilter`. Only supports gRPC. Calls `checkRequestUtils::createTcpCheck()` and sends the check on `onNewConnection()`.\n- **`source/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/config.h` / `.cc`**: Factory for the TCP filter, registered as `envoy.filters.network.ext_authz`.\n\n### Supporting\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/mutation_rules/mutation_rules.h` / `.cc`**: `Checker` class that validates header mutations against configurable rules (allow/disallow specific header operations).\n\n## 4. Failure Modes\n\n### 4.1 Authorization Service Unavailable / Timeout\n\n**Trigger**: The authz service cluster is unreachable, the gRPC call fails, or the HTTP request to the authz service returns 5xx or times out.\n\n**Behavior**: The `Client` returns `CheckStatus::Error`.\n\n- If `failure_mode_allow: true` (fail-open): The request is **allowed through**. The `failure_mode_allowed` counter is incremented. If `failure_mode_allow_header_add: true`, an `x-envoy-auth-failure-mode-allowed: true` header is added to the request so the upstream knows the authz check was skipped.\n- If `failure_mode_allow: false` (fail-closed, **default**): The request is **rejected** with a local reply. The status code is `status_on_error` (default: 403 Forbidden). The response detail is `ext_authz_error`. The `UnauthorizedExternalService` response flag is set.\n- For gRPC error responses with `error_response` present, custom status code, body, headers_to_set, and headers_to_append from the error response are applied (if `validate_mutations` passes).\n\n**Stats incremented**: `error`, and (if applicable) `failure_mode_allowed`.\n\n### 4.2 Authorization Denied\n\n**Trigger**: The authz server explicitly denies the request (non-OK gRPC status without `error_response`, or non-200/non-5xx HTTP status).\n\n**Behavior**: A local reply is sent to the client with:\n- Status code from the `DeniedHttpResponse` (default 403).\n- Body from the denial response (truncated to `max_denied_response_body_bytes` if set).\n- Headers from the denial response's `headers_to_set` field.\n- The `UnauthorizedExternalService` response flag is set. Response detail: `ext_authz_denied`.\n\n**Stats incremented**: `denied`.\n\n### 4.3 Cluster Removed (CDS)\n\n**Trigger**: The authz cluster configured in `http_service.server_uri.cluster` is removed via CDS while the filter is running.\n\n**Behavior** (HTTP client): `RawHttpClientImpl::check()` returns an error response immediately when `cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(cluster)` returns `nullptr`. This is treated as `CheckStatus::Error`.\n\n### 4.4 Invalid Authz Response\n\n**Trigger**: The authz server returns headers or query parameters that fail validation (when `validate_mutations: true`), such as invalid header names/values or invalid URL-encoded query parameters.\n\n**Behavior**: The request is rejected with 500 Internal Server Error. Response detail: `ext_authz_invalid`. The `invalid` stat is incremented.\n\n### 4.5 Response Header Limits Exceeded\n\n**Trigger**: Mutations from the authz response would cause request or response headers to exceed the configured header count or byte-size limits.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- For request header mutations: If `headersWithinLimits()` fails after a mutation, the response is rejected (500). `request_header_limits_reached` stat is incremented.\n- For response header mutations (encode path): If `enforce_response_header_limits: true` and limits are exceeded, a 500 local reply is sent. `response_header_limits_reached` stat is incremented.\n- For denied/error responses: Excess headers are silently dropped when `enforce_response_header_limits: true`. `omitted_response_headers` stat is incremented.\n\n### 4.6 Filter Disabled\n\n**Trigger**: `filter_enabled` evaluates to false (runtime fractional percent) or `filter_enabled_metadata` doesn't match.\n\n**Behavior**: If `deny_at_disable: true`, the request is denied (status = `status_on_error`). Otherwise, the filter is bypassed and the request continues. The `disabled` stat is incremented.\n\n### 4.7 Per-Route Service Override Failure\n\n**Trigger**: A per-route `grpc_service` or `http_service` override is configured but the client creation fails.\n\n**Behavior**: Falls back to the default (globally configured) authz client. A warning-level log is emitted.\n\n### 4.8 Request Destroyed Mid-Call\n\n**Trigger**: The downstream connection is closed or the stream is reset while the authz check is in flight.\n\n**Behavior**: `Filter::onDestroy()` calls `client_->cancel()` to cancel the in-flight gRPC or HTTP request if the state is `State::Calling`.\n\n## 5. Testing\n\n### Unit Tests\n\n| Test File | Scope |\n|---|---|\n| `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_test.cc` | Core HTTP filter unit tests. Tests `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, `onComplete()` for all response types (OK, Denied, Error). Tests header mutations, query parameter mutations, per-route config, `failure_mode_allow`, dynamic metadata, body buffering, and validation. Parametrized over gRPC/HTTP client types. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config_test.cc` | Config factory tests. Tests proto validation, factory creation for gRPC and HTTP service configs. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl_test.cc` | gRPC client implementation tests. Tests `check()`, `onSuccess()`, `onFailure()`, response parsing, tracing tag setting. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl_test.cc` | HTTP client implementation tests. Tests request construction, response parsing, header matching, cluster-not-found handling. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/check_request_utils_test.cc` | Tests `CheckRequest` protobuf construction from HTTP/TCP request attributes. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/ext_authz_test.cc` | TCP filter unit tests. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/config_test.cc` | TCP filter config factory tests. |\n\n### Integration Tests\n\n| Test File | Scope |\n|---|---|\n| `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_integration_test.cc` | End-to-end tests with a real gRPC authz server. Tests OK/Denied/Error flows, header mutations, body buffering, failure mode, metadata, timeouts, response header limits, per-route overrides. Parametrized over IP version, gRPC client type, and filter config variants. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/ext_authz_integration_test.cc` | End-to-end tests for the TCP filter with a real gRPC server. |\n\n### Fuzz Tests\n\n| Test File | Scope |\n|---|---|\n| `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_fuzz_test.cc` | Fuzz testing for the gRPC filter path. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_fuzz_test.cc` | Fuzz testing for the HTTP filter path. |\n| `test/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/ext_authz_fuzz_test.cc` | Fuzz testing for the TCP filter. |\n\n### Test Mocks\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/mocks.h` / `.cc`**: Mock `Client` implementation for unit testing the filter without a real authz server.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/test_common.h` / `.cc`**: Shared test utilities.\n\n### Running Tests\n\nTests are built and run via Bazel:\n```bash\n# HTTP filter unit tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz:ext_authz_test\n\n# HTTP filter integration tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz:ext_authz_integration_test\n\n# Common library tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz:...\n\n# TCP filter tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz:...\n```\n\n## 6. Debugging\n\n### Stats / Metrics\n\nThe filter emits counters under the prefix `ext_authz.<stat_prefix>.` (where `stat_prefix` is configurable, default empty yields `ext_authz.`):\n\n| Stat Name | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `ok` | Requests approved by the authz service. |\n| `denied` | Requests denied by the authz service. |\n| `error` | Authz service returned an error or was unreachable. |\n| `disabled` | Requests where the filter was disabled (via `filter_enabled`). |\n| `failure_mode_allowed` | Requests allowed through despite authz errors (fail-open). |\n| `invalid` | Responses rejected due to invalid mutations (`validate_mutations`). |\n| `ignored_dynamic_metadata` | Dynamic metadata from authz ignored (`enable_dynamic_metadata_ingestion: false`). |\n| `filter_state_name_collision` | Filter state key collision (another filter already set data at this name). |\n| `omitted_response_headers` | Response headers from authz that were dropped due to header limits. |\n| `request_header_limits_reached` | Request header mutations exceeded limits. |\n| `response_header_limits_reached` | Response header mutations exceeded limits. |\n\nWhen `charge_cluster_response_stats: true` (default), the filter also charges per-cluster stats under the authz cluster's scope: `ext_authz.ok`, `ext_authz.denied`, `ext_authz.error`, `ext_authz.invalid`, `ext_authz.failure_mode_allowed`.\n\n**Key diagnostic**: A spike in `error` + `failure_mode_allowed` indicates authz service instability. A spike in `denied` may indicate a policy change or misconfiguration. Monitor `invalid` if `validate_mutations` is enabled.\n\n### Logging\n\nThe filter uses the `ext_authz` log component (`Logger::Id::ext_authz`). Enable trace-level logging with:\n```\n--component-log-level ext_authz:trace\n```\n\nKey log messages:\n- `trace`: \"ext_authz filter calling authorization server.\" -- call initiated.\n- `trace`: \"ext_authz filter added header(s) to the request/response\" -- header mutations applied.\n- `debug`: \"ext_authz filter is buffering the request\" -- body buffering started.\n- `debug`: \"ext_authz is clearing route cache\" -- route cache cleared after header mutations.\n- `trace`: \"ext_authz filter allowed the request with error\" -- fail-open triggered.\n- `trace`: \"ext_authz filter rejected the request. Response status code: ...\" -- request denied.\n- `warn`: \"ext_authz filter: failed to create per-route gRPC/HTTP client...\" -- per-route client creation failure.\n\nFor the HTTP client, relevant logs are under `Logger::Id::config`.\nFor the gRPC client, relevant logs are under `Logger::Id::ext_authz`.\n\n### Tracing\n\nThe filter propagates tracing spans to the authz service call. The gRPC client passes the parent span to the async gRPC call. The HTTP client creates a child span named `async <cluster_name> egress`.\n\nTrace tags set by the filter:\n- `ext_authz_status`: `ext_authz_ok`, `ext_authz_unauthorized`, or `ext_authz_error`.\n- `ext_authz_http_status`: HTTP status code (HTTP client only).\n\n### Filter State\n\nWhen `emit_filter_state_stats: true` or `filter_metadata` is configured, the filter stores `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` in the request's filter state (keyed by the filter config name). This object exposes:\n- `latency_us`: Latency of the authz call in microseconds.\n- `bytesSent` / `bytesReceived`: Wire bytes for the authz call (gRPC via Envoy gRPC only).\n- `clusterInfo`: The authz cluster info.\n- `upstreamHost`: The specific authz host that handled the request.\n- `grpcStatus`: The gRPC status code from the authz response.\n\nThese values are accessible from access log formatters that support filter state field lookup.\n\n### Response Flags\n\nThe filter sets the `UF` (UnauthorizedExternalService) response flag when a request is denied or encounters an error. This appears in access logs as `UF`.\n\n### Response Code Details\n\n| Detail String | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `ext_authz_denied` | Request was explicitly denied by the authz service. |\n| `ext_authz_error` | Authz service returned an error and fail-closed is active. |\n| `ext_authz_invalid` | Authz response contained invalid mutations. |\n\n### Dynamic Metadata\n\nOn OK responses, the authz server can inject dynamic metadata under the `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` namespace. This metadata includes an auto-added `ext_authz_duration` field (in milliseconds) and any metadata from the authz response's `dynamic_metadata` field. Other filters (rate limiting, routing, access logging) can consume this metadata.\n\n### Common Debugging Workflow\n\n1. Check stats: Look at `ext_authz.ok`, `ext_authz.denied`, `ext_authz.error` to understand the distribution of outcomes.\n2. Check access logs: Look for the `UF` response flag and `ext_authz_denied`/`ext_authz_error` response code details.\n3. Enable trace logging: Set `--component-log-level ext_authz:trace` to see the full request/response flow.\n4. Check the authz server: Verify the authz cluster is healthy via admin endpoint (`/clusters`). Look for connection failures, timeouts, or 5xx responses.\n5. Check tracing: Use distributed tracing to see the authz call latency and status tags.\n6. Check filter state: If `emit_filter_state_stats` is enabled, inspect latency and bytes via access log formatters.\n7. For header mutation issues: Enable `validate_mutations: true` and monitor `invalid` stats. Check trace logs for \"Rejected invalid header\" or \"Ignoring invalid header\" messages.\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/onboarding.md
# ext_authz Filter Handoff Document

## 1. Purpose

The ext_authz filter is an **external authorization** filter for Envoy that delegates request authorization decisions to an external service. It exists as both an **HTTP filter** (`envoy.filters.http.ext_authz`) and a **network (TCP) filter** (`envoy.filters.network.ext_authz`), both sharing a common client library.

### What it does

Before a request reaches the upstream service, the ext_authz filter intercepts it and sends an authorization check request (a `CheckRequest` protobuf) to a configurable external authorization server. The authz server inspects request attributes (headers, path, source/destination IPs, TLS info, request body, metadata) and returns one of three verdicts:

- **OK**: The request is authorized. The authz server can optionally mutate request headers, add/remove query parameters, set response headers, and inject dynamic metadata.
- **Denied**: The request is rejected. The filter sends a local reply (configurable status code, body, and headers) back to the client without forwarding to the upstream.
- **Error**: The authz server was unreachable or returned an error. Behavior depends on the `failure_mode_allow` configuration (fail-open vs. fail-closed).

### When to use it

- Enforcing authorization policies (RBAC, OPA, custom authz logic) external to Envoy.
- Integrating with third-party authz systems (e.g., Open Policy Agent, Istio authz).
- Adding per-request authentication/authorization without modifying application code.
- Implementing request enrichment -- the authz server can add headers, modify query params, and inject metadata on approved requests.

### Communication Modes

The filter supports two backend protocols for communicating with the authz service:

1. **gRPC** (`grpc_service`): Use
